
############################################################
I'm experimenting with a program to understand how input conditions influence its worst-case performance, particularly in terms of finding the longest execution path as the input size increases. By conducting a worst-case analysis, I aim to identify constraints that define a valid input set at different input sizes (N). So far, I have found one possible set of correct constraints/conditions (not the only one) that characterize such valid inputs. Here they are:

The constraints for input (N=1):

None


The constraints for input (N=2):

(assert  ( <  in0 in1))


The constraints for input (N=3):

(assert  ( <  in0 in2))


The constraints for input (N=4):

(assert (and  ( <  in0 in3)  ( <  in1 in2)))


The constraints for input (N=5):

(assert (and  ( <  in0 in4)  ( <  in1 in3)))


The constraints for input (N=6):

(assert (and (and  ( <  in0 in5)  ( <  in1 in4))  ( <  in2 in3)))


The constraints for input (N=7):

(assert (and (and  ( <  in0 in6)  ( <  in1 in5))  ( <  in2 in4)))


The constraints for input (N=8):

(assert (and (and (and  ( <  in0 in7)  ( <  in1 in6))  ( <  in2 in5))  ( <  in3 in4)))


The constraints for input (N=9):

(assert (and (and (and  ( <  in0 in8)  ( <  in1 in7))  ( <  in2 in6))  ( <  in3 in5)))


The constraints for input (N=10):

(assert (and (and (and (and  ( <  in0 in9)  ( <  in1 in8))  ( <  in2 in7))  ( <  in3 in6))  ( <  in4 in5)))


Here is more context for you to generalize the constraints better. Below is the source code for the SPF problem:

```java
package own;

import gov.nasa.jpf.symbc.Debug;

public class ComplexPalindrome {

    public static void algo(int[] a) {
        boolean fail = false;
        boolean skip = false;
        final int N = a.length;
        for (int i = 0; i < Math.floor(N/2); i++) {
            int point = N - i - 1;
            if (a[i] < a[point]){
                // Skip
                skip = true;
            } else {
                fail = true;
            }
        }
        if (!fail) {
            int aa = 99999;
            for (int i = 0; i < N; i++) {
                aa = aa*aa;
            }
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        final int N = Integer.parseInt(args[0]);

        int a[] = new int[N];
        for (int i = 0; i < N; i++) {
            a[i] = Debug.makeSymbolicInteger("in"+i);
        }

        // We only measure the complexity of this function itself.
        algo(a);
    }
}

```


Generalize what makes the set of constraints valid such that we can recover a valid set for N inputs. Provide a Python function that outputs a valid SMT-LIB format assert constraint string for all values of N in SMT-LIB format, matching the format of the examples provided. Ensure the constraints are in canonical form. Don't overfit the data here but also don't oversimplify to the point of trivialness. Make sure none of the given examples contradict your generalization.```

Each inequality should be in the form '(assert (op x y))', where `x` and `y` are variables, constants, or formulas of variables/constants, and `op` is an operation or inequality (e.g., `=`, `<`, `<=`, `>`, `>=`, `and`, etc.).

Structure your response in the following format and use this code template:

CASUAL:
[CASUAL EXPLAINATION HERE]

FORMAL:
```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    # Do some logic here to return a SMT-LIB Format String e.g. (assert (and (op1 x y) (op2 x z)))

    return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)

Example 1:

CASUAL: 'Constraints grow with N'

FORMAL: ```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str: 
 if N == 1:
 return ""
 else:
 constraints = ""
 for i in range(1, N+1):
 constraints += f"(assert (<= x{i} 100))
"
return constraints

return constraints
N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)
############################################################
CASUAL: '[General observation]: As N increases, the constraints become more complex by adding inequalities and ensuring each variable is less than the next N-1 variables. This maintains that there's no cycle, all variables are distinct, and each variable is greater than the 'opposite' one at a distance of N / 2.'

FORMAL:
```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(1, N+1):
            constraints += f"(assert (<= {chr(97 + N - 1)} {chr(97 + i - 1)}))\n"
        constraints += f"(assert (<= {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + i)}))\n"
        for i in range(1, (N//2)+1):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + N - 1 - 2*i)} {chr(97 + i - 1)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)
```

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            if ((i + 1) % (N // 2)) != 0:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
        for i in range(N // 2):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + N - 1 - i)} {chr(97 + i)}))\n"
        return constraints

```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            if i != 0:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i - 1))}))\n"
        if N % 2 == 1:
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + 0)} {chr(97 + (N - 1))}))\n"
        else:
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + 0)} {chr(97 + 1)}))\n"
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 2))} {chr(97 + (N - 1))}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)
```

CASUAL:
'[New observation]: For each N, the constraints correctly place each variable less than its successor by using a Cyclic Ordering, ensuring that the variables form a strictly decreasing chain. Special cases for middle variable and its neighbors are only needed when N is odd or even, respectively, to maintain the strictly decreasing order throughout.]

FORMAL:
```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
        if N % 2 == 1:
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 1))} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)
```

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            if i != N-1:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
        if N % 2 == 1:
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + 0)} {chr(97 + (N - 1))}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))

print(constraints)

```python
def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            if i != N-1:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
            if i == N//2 and N % 2 == 1:  # Check if N is odd
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 1))} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))

print(constraints)

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
        if N % 2 == 1:
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 1))} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            if i != N-1:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + (i + 1))}))\n"
            if i == 0 and N % 2 == 1:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 1))} {chr(97 + 2)})\n"
            if i == N-1 and N % 2 == 1:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))
constraints = generate_constraints(N)
print(constraints)
```

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N - 1):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + i + 1)}))\n"
            if N % 2 == 1 and i == (N - 2) // 2:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + (N - 1))} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints

N = int(input("N="))

print(constraints)

def generate_constraints(N: int) -> str:

    if N == 1:
        return ""
    else:
        constraints = ""
        for i in range(N):
            constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + i)} {chr(97 + ((i + 1) % N))}))\n"
            if N % 2 == 1 and i == N // 2:
                constraints += f"(assert (< {chr(97 + N - 1)} {chr(97 + 0)}))\n"
        return constraints
